            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             10. SP David Price, Tampa Bay Rays
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="10. SP David Price, Tampa Bay Rays" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/003/165/918/hi-res-168439919_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              J. Meric/Getty Images
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            As reigning AL Cy Young winner, David Price could wind up being the biggest trade chip to hit the block since the Mariners dealt a 29-year-old Ken Griffey Jr. to the Reds back in 2000. Price is not a free agent until 2016, but he's already making $10.1 million, and the Rays won't be able to afford him much longer.
           </p>
           <p>
            That said, he's done little to boost his value so far in 2013, going 1-4 with a 5.24 ERA and 10.6 H/9 over his first nine starts. Making matters worse, he suffered a
            <a href="http://espn.go.com/mlb/story/_/id/9280020/david-price-tampa-bay-rays-injures-left-triceps-leaves-game-boston-red-sox">
             strained left triceps
            </a>
            on Wednesday night against Boston, and he will likely miss his next start.
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Stock:
            </strong>
            Down
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-43 cf display-none " data-page="43">
          <header class="article_page-header">

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             9. 1B Joey Votto, Cincinnati Reds
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="9. 1B Joey Votto, Cincinnati Reds" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/003/165/919/hi-res-168537595_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              Jamie Sabau/Getty Images
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            Had it not been for July knee surgery that wound up costing him roughly two months, Joey Votto very well might have won his second NL MVP award last season. As it was, he still managed to lead the NL with a .474 on-base percentage thanks to 94 walks.
           </p>
           <p>
            He's never going to have 40-HR power, but he has the best plate discipline in all of baseball and continues to be a force in the middle of a very good Reds lineup. He's currently hitting .327/.457/.473 with a league-high 34 walks, though he has just 17 RBI.
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Stock:
            </strong>
            Even
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-44 cf display-none " data-page="44">
          <header class="article_page-header">
           <div class="article_nav-bar br-texture--sudo br-texture--sudo-fade-to-white">
            <div class="paginators paginators--top">
             <a class="paginator paginator--secondary paginator--prev" href="javascript: void(0)" title="Previous Page">

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             8. SP Felix Hernandez, Seattle Mariners
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="8. SP Felix Hernandez, Seattle Mariners" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/003/165/920/hi-res-168310911_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              Joe Sargent/Getty Images
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            Signed to a then-record seven-year, $175 million deal this offseason, Felix Hernandez has been one of the game's most dynamic arms since breaking into the league as a 19-year-old back in 2005.
           </p>
           <p>
            It's a crime that he's gone just 40-35 over the past three seasons, but he is the poster boy for a win-loss record being a poor determinant of how good a pitcher really is. Over that span, he has a 2.92 ERA, 1.138 WHIP and has thrown an impressive 715.1 innings. Still just 27, he'll be a big part of the Mariners' return to contention in the not-too-distant future.
           </p>
           <p>
            He's 5-2 with an AL-best 1.53 ERA so far this season.
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Stock:
            </strong>
            Up
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-45 cf display-none " data-page="45">
          <header class="article_page-header">
           <div class="article_nav-bar br-texture--sudo br-texture--sudo-fade-to-white">

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             7. 2B Robinson Cano, New York Yankees
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="7. 2B Robinson Cano, New York Yankees" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/003/165/921/hi-res-168749532_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              Elsa/Getty Images
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            Seemingly the only healthy player on the Yankees roster entering the season, Robinson Cano posted career highs last season with 33 home runs and a .929 OPS, as he has been relied upon more and more to be a leader in the middle of the offense.
           </p>
           <p>
            In the final year of his contract, the 30-year-old Cano is headed for a huge payday this offseason, and he has done nothing to hurt his value so far. He's currently hitting .301/.345/.552 with 10 home runs and 25 RBI for a surprisingly good, albeit injury-depleted, Yankees team.
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Stock:
            </strong>
            Up
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-46 cf display-none " data-page="46">
          <header class="article_page-header">
           <div class="article_nav-bar br-texture--sudo br-texture--sudo-fade-to-white">

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             6. C Buster Posey, San Francisco Giants
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="6. C Buster Posey, San Francisco Giants" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/003/165/922/hi-res-167516732_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              Ezra Shaw/Getty Images
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            The Giants are 2-for-2 on World Series titles when they have Buster Posey for a full season. That may be a ridiculous stat, but it does speak to just how valuable the young backstop has been so far in his career and how much success he has already enjoyed.
           </p>
           <p>
            The reigning NL MVP was locked up on a nine-year, $167 million deal in late March, and he continues to be the Giants' biggest offensive threat. He's not quite matching the .336 average he sported when he won the NL batting title last season, but he is hitting a solid .286/.391/.508 with five home runs and 25 RBI so far in 2013.
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Stock:
            </strong>
            Even
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-47 cf display-none " data-page="47">
          <header class="article_page-header">
           <div class="article_nav-bar br-texture--sudo br-texture--sudo-fade-to-white">

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             5. LF Ryan Braun, Milwaukee Brewers
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="5. LF Ryan Braun, Milwaukee Brewers" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/003/165/923/hi-res-167108560_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              Mike McGinnis/Getty Images
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            Despite an offseason filled with PED controversy, Ryan Braun came out and turned in another MVP-caliber season in 2012. In posting his second-straight 30/30 season, Braun led the NL with 41 home runs and a .987 OPS, finishing second in MVP voting to Buster Posey.
           </p>
           <p>
            He's been without Corey Hart and Aramis Ramirez protecting him in the lineup for most of the season so far, but he has still managed to hit .315/.403/.592 with eight home runs and 26 RBI. He's also an absolute bargain this year at $9.5 million, making him that much more valuable.
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Stock:
            </strong>
            Up
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-48 cf display-none " data-page="48">
          <header class="article_page-header">
           <div class="article_nav-bar br-texture--sudo br-texture--sudo-fade-to-white">
            <div class="paginators paginators--top">

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             4. SP Clayton Kershaw, Los Angeles Dodgers
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="4. SP Clayton Kershaw, Los Angeles Dodgers" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/003/165/924/hi-res-168334175_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              Stephen Dunn/Getty Images
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            After capturing NL Cy Young honors in 2011 with a 21-5, 2.28 ERA, 248 K performance that also won him the pitching Triple Crown, Clayton Kershaw very well could have taken home Cy Young honors again last season when he led the NL with a 2.53 ERA.
           </p>
           <p>
            With Felix Hernandez and Justin Verlander signing long-term deals this offseason, Kershaw will be the next big-time arm to get paid, and he could be baseball's first $200 million pitcher. It's hard to argue with his numbers, as he's 4-2 with an MLB-best 1.40 ERA on the year. Oh, and he's still only 25 years old.
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Stock:
            </strong>
            Up
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-49 cf display-none " data-page="49">
          <header class="article_page-header">
           <div class="article_nav-bar br-texture--sudo br-texture--sudo-fade-to-white">

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             3. LF Mike Trout, Los Angeles Angels
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="3. LF Mike Trout, Los Angeles Angels" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/003/165/925/hi-res-168055611_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              Jeff Gross/Getty Images
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            As a 20-year-old last season, Mike Trout turned in a rookie year for the ages. Despite not being called up until the team's 20th game of the season, he hit .326/.399/.564 with 30 home runs and posted AL-bests of 49 steals and 129 runs scored.
           </p>
           <p>
            That set the bar impossibly high for the young star, but he has managed to avoid a drastic fall-off so far in his sophomore campaign. He's currently hitting .293/.364/.549 with eight home runs and seven steals, and while that may not make him the third best player in the game, they're fantastic numbers nonetheless.
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Stock:
            </strong>
            Even
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             2. SP Justin Verlander, Detroit Tigers
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="2. SP Justin Verlander, Detroit Tigers" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/003/165/926/hi-res-168114219_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              Bob Levey/Getty Images
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            Now the highest-paid pitcher in baseball history after signing a seven-year, $180 million deal in March, Justin Verlander continues to be the gold standard on the mound
            <span class="st">
             
            </span>
            though Clayton Kershaw is right there with him at this point.
           </p>
           <p>
            The 30-year-old Verlander followed up his MVP season in 2011 with another great year last year, going 17-8 with a 2.64 ERA over an AL-high 238.1 innings to finish second in Cy Young voting.
           </p>
           <p>
            It's been more of the same from him so far this season, as he's 4-3 with a 1.93 ERA and 10.0 K/9 over his first eight starts.
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Stock:
            </strong>
            Up
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-51 cf display-none " data-page="51">
          <header class="article_page-header">
           <div class="article_nav-bar br-texture--sudo br-texture--sudo-fade-to-white">
            <div class="paginators paginators--top">

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             1. 3B Miguel Cabrera, Detroit Tigers
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="1. 3B Miguel Cabrera, Detroit Tigers" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/003/165/927/hi-res-167106263_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              Victor Decolongon/Getty Images
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            Long one of the most consistent all-around offensive players in the game, Miguel Cabrera took things to another level last season when he hit .330 with 44 home runs and 139 RBI to become the first Triple Crown winner since Carl Yastrzemski in 1967.
           </p>
           <p>
            That would be a hard act for most to follow, but Cabrera has been an absolute beast once again in 2013, and he seems poised to make another run at the Triple Crown. He's currently hitting .369 with eight home runs and an AL-high 41 RBI, and he remains the top player in the game today.
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Stock:
            </strong>
            Up
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>

    // Load the SDK asynchronously
    (function(){
        // If we've already installed the SDK, we're done
        if (document.getElementById('facebook-jssdk')) {return;}

        // Get the first script element, which we'll use to find the parent node
        var firstScriptElement = document.getElementsByTagName('script')[0];

        // Create a new script element and set its id
        var facebookJS = document.createElement('script');
        facebookJS.id = 'facebook-jssdk';

        // Set the new script's source to the source of the Facebook JS SDK

        // Insert the Facebook JS SDK into the DOM

    }());
